     <p><span class="error" style="display:none">HIDDEN ERROR: Usage of "relatives" is not recognized</span></p> 
     <p><b>Ravi Shankar</b>, <a href="/wiki/KBE" title="KBE" class="mw-redirect">KBE</a> (<small>IPA:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Bengali" title="Help:IPA for Bengali">[?r?bi ????k?r]</a></span>; 7 April 1920&nbsp;– 11 December 2012), born Rabindra Shankar Chowdhury (<a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>&nbsp;: ???????? ????? ??????),<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip48_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip48-2">[2]</a></sup> his name often preceded by the title <a href="/wiki/Pandit" title="Pandit">Pandit</a> ('Master'), was an <a href="/wiki/Music_of_India" title="Music of India">Indian musician</a> and a composer of <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_classical_music" title="Hindustani classical music">Hindustani classical music</a>. He was one of the best-known exponents of the <a href="/wiki/Sitar" title="Sitar">sitar</a> in the second half of the 20th century and influenced many other musicians throughout the world.</p> 
     <p>Shankar was born to a <a href="/wiki/Bengali_people" title="Bengali people" class="mw-redirect">Bengali</a> family in India,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> and spent his youth touring India and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> with the dance group of his brother <a href="/wiki/Uday_Shankar" title="Uday Shankar">Uday Shankar</a>. He gave up dancing in 1938 to study sitar playing under court musician <a href="/wiki/Allauddin_Khan" title="Allauddin Khan">Allauddin Khan</a>. After finishing his studies in 1944, Shankar worked as a composer, creating the music for the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Apu_Trilogy" title="The Apu Trilogy">Apu Trilogy</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Satyajit_Ray" title="Satyajit Ray">Satyajit Ray</a>, and was music director of <a href="/wiki/All_India_Radio" title="All India Radio">All India Radio</a>, New Delhi, from 1949 to 1956.</p> 
     <p>In 1956 he began to tour Europe and the Americas playing <a href="/wiki/Indian_classical_music" title="Indian classical music">Indian classical music</a> and increased its popularity there in the 1960s through teaching, performance, and his association with violinist <a href="/wiki/Yehudi_Menuhin" title="Yehudi Menuhin">Yehudi Menuhin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beatles" title="Beatles" class="mw-redirect">Beatles</a> guitarist <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a>. His influence on the latter helped popularize the <a href="/wiki/Raga_rock" title="Raga rock">use of Indian instruments in pop music</a> throughout the 1960s. Shankar engaged Western music by writing compositions for sitar and orchestra, and toured the world in the 1970s and 1980s. From 1986 to 1992, he served as a nominated member of Rajya Sabha, the upper chamber of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Parliament" title="Indian Parliament" class="mw-redirect">Parliament of India</a>. He continued to perform up until the end of his life. In 1999, Shankar was awarded India's highest civilian honour, the <a href="/wiki/Bharat_Ratna" title="Bharat Ratna">Bharat Ratna</a>.</p> 
     <p></p>

     <p></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p>Shankar was born on 7 April 1920 in Varanasi, India, to a Bengali family, as the youngest of seven brothers.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip48_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip48-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AMG_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMG-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Massey_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Massey-5">[5]</a></sup> His father, Shyam Shankar, was a <a href="/wiki/Middle_Temple" title="Middle Temple">Middle Temple</a> <a href="/wiki/Barrister" title="Barrister">barrister</a> and scholar from <a href="/wiki/East_Bengal" title="East Bengal">East Bengal</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>). A respected statesman, lawyer and politician, he served for several years as <i><a href="/wiki/Dewan" title="Dewan">dewan</a></i> (chief minister) of <a href="/wiki/Jhalawar" title="Jhalawar">Jhalawar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan" title="Rajasthan">Rajasthan</a>, and used the <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> spelling of the family name and removed its last part.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip48_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip48-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ghoshp7_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghoshp7-6">[6]</a></sup> Shyam was married to Hemangini Devi who hailed from a small village named Nasrathpur in Mardah block of <a href="/wiki/Ghazipur_district" title="Ghazipur district">Ghazipur district</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">Benares</a>, and her father was a prosperous landlord. Shyam later worked as a lawyer in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip48_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip48-2">[2]</a></sup> and there he married a second time while Devi raised Shankar in Varanasi, and did not meet his son until he was eight years old.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip48_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip48-2">[2]</a></sup> Shankar shortened the Sanskrit version of his first name, Ravindra, to Ravi, for "sun".<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip48_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip48-2">[2]</a></sup> Shankar had six siblings, only four of whom lived past infancy: <a href="/wiki/Uday_Shankar" title="Uday Shankar">Uday</a> (who became a famous choreographer and dancer), Rajendra, Debendra and Bhupendra. Shankar attended the Bengalitola High School in Benares between 1927 and 1928.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>At the age of ten, after spending his first decade in Varanasi, Shankar went to Paris with the dance group of his brother, choreographer Uday Shankar.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGrove_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGrove-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ghoshp55_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghoshp55-9">[9]</a></sup> By the age of 13 he had become a member of the group, accompanied its members on tour and learned to dance and play various Indian instruments.<sup id="cite_ref-AMG_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMG-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Massey_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Massey-5">[5]</a></sup> Uday's dance group toured Europe and the United States in the early to mid-1930s and Shankar learned French, discovered Western classical music, jazz, cinema and became acquainted with Western customs.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip50_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip50-10">[10]</a></sup> Shankar heard the lead musician for the <a href="/wiki/Maihar" title="Maihar">Maihar</a> court, Allauddin Khan, in December 1934 at a music conference in <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a> and Uday convinced the Maharaja of Maihar in 1935 to allow Khan to become his group's soloist for a tour of Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip50_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip50-10">[10]</a></sup> Shankar was sporadically trained by Khan on tour, and Khan offered Shankar training to become a serious musician under the condition that he abandon touring and come to Maihar.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip50_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip50-10">[10]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Training_and_work_in_India">Training and work in India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Training and work in India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Shankar's parents had died by the time he returned from the European tour, and touring the West had become difficult because of political conflicts that would lead to <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip51_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip51-11">[11]</a></sup> Shankar gave up his dancing career in 1938 to go to <a href="/wiki/Maihar" title="Maihar">Maihar</a> and study <a href="/wiki/Indian_classical_music" title="Indian classical music">Indian classical music</a> as Khan's pupil, living with his family in the traditional <i><a href="/wiki/Gurukul" title="Gurukul" class="mw-redirect">gurukul</a></i> system.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGrove_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGrove-8">[8]</a></sup> Khan was a rigorous teacher and Shankar had training on <i>sitar</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Surbahar" title="Surbahar">surbahar</a></i>, learned <i><a href="/wiki/Raga" title="Raga">ragas</a></i> and the musical styles <i><a href="/wiki/Dhrupad" title="Dhrupad">dhrupad</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dhamar_(music)" title="Dhamar (music)">dhamar</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Khyal" title="Khyal">khyal</a></i>, and was taught the techniques of the instruments <i><a href="/wiki/Rudra_veena" title="Rudra veena">rudra veena</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rubab_(instrument)" title="Rubab (instrument)">rubab</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Sursingar" title="Sursingar">sursingar</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGrove_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGrove-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip52_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip52-12">[12]</a></sup> He often studied with Khan's children <a href="/wiki/Ali_Akbar_Khan" title="Ali Akbar Khan">Ali Akbar Khan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Annapurna_Devi" title="Annapurna Devi">Annapurna Devi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip51_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip51-11">[11]</a></sup> Shankar began to perform publicly on <i>sitar</i> in December 1939 and his debut performance was a <i><a href="/wiki/Jugalbandi" title="Jugalbandi">jugalbandi</a></i> (duet) with Ali Akbar Khan, who played the string instrument <i><a href="/wiki/Sarod" title="Sarod">sarod</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip53_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip53-13">[13]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Shankar completed his training in 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-AMG_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMG-4">[4]</a></sup> he moved to <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a> and joined the <a href="/wiki/Indian_People%27s_Theatre_Association" title="Indian People's Theatre Association">Indian People's Theatre Association</a>, for whom he composed music for ballets in 1945 and 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-AMG_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMG-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ghoshp57_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghoshp57-14">[14]</a></sup> Shankar recomposed the music for the popular song "<a href="/wiki/Sare_Jahan_Se_Achcha" title="Sare Jahan Se Achcha" class="mw-redirect">Sare Jahan Se Achcha</a>" at the age of 25.<sup id="cite_ref-Sharma_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sharma-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Arunabha_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arunabha-16">[16]</a></sup> He began to record music for <a href="/wiki/HMV_Group" title="HMV Group" class="mw-redirect">HMV</a> India and worked as a music director for <a href="/wiki/All_India_Radio" title="All India Radio">All India Radio</a> (AIR), New Delhi, from February 1949 to January 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-AMG_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMG-4">[4]</a></sup> Shankar founded the Indian National Orchestra at AIR and composed for it; in his compositions he combined Western and classical Indian instrumentation.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip56_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip56-17">[17]</a></sup> Beginning in the mid-1950s he composed the music for the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Apu_Trilogy" title="The Apu Trilogy">Apu Trilogy</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Satyajit_Ray" title="Satyajit Ray">Satyajit Ray</a>, which became internationally acclaimed.<sup id="cite_ref-Massey_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Massey-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> He was music director for several Hindi movies including <i><a href="/wiki/Godaan" title="Godaan">Godaan</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Anuradha_(1960_film)" title="Anuradha (1960 film)"><i>Anuradha</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1956.E2.80.9369:_International_career">1956–69: International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1956–69: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/V._K._Narayana_Menon" title="V. K. Narayana Menon">V. K. Narayana Menon</a>, director of AIR Delhi, introduced the Western violinist Yehudi Menuhin to Shankar during Menuhin's first visit to India in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip47_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip47-20">[20]</a></sup> Shankar had performed as part of a cultural delegation in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> in 1954 and Menuhin invited Shankar in 1955 to perform in New York City for a demonstration of Indian classical music, sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Foundation" title="Ford Foundation">Ford Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip57_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip57-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip58_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip58-22">[22]</a></sup> Shankar declined to attend because of problems in his marriage, but recommended Ali Akbar Khan to play instead.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip58_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip58-22">[22]</a></sup> Khan reluctantly accepted and performed with <i><a href="/wiki/Tabla" title="Tabla">tabla</a></i> (percussion) player <a href="/wiki/Chatur_Lal" title="Chatur Lal">Chatur Lal</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Modern_Art" title="Museum of Modern Art">Museum of Modern Art</a>, and he later became the first Indian classical musician to perform on American television and record a full <i>raga</i> performance, for <a href="/wiki/Angel_Records" title="Angel Records">Angel Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip5859_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip5859-23">[23]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Shankar heard about the positive response Khan received and resigned from AIR in 1956 to tour the United Kingdom, Germany, and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip61_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip61-24">[24]</a></sup> He played for smaller audiences and educated them about Indian music, incorporating <i>ragas</i> from the <a href="/wiki/South_India" title="South India">South Indian</a> <a href="/wiki/Carnatic_music" title="Carnatic music">Carnatic music</a> in his performances, and recorded his first <a href="/wiki/LP_album" title="LP album" class="mw-redirect">LP album</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Three_Ragas" title="Three Ragas">Three Ragas</a></i> in London, released in 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip61_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip61-24">[24]</a></sup> In 1958, Shankar participated in the celebrations of the tenth anniversary of the United Nations and <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> music festival in Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghoshp57_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghoshp57-14">[14]</a></sup> From 1961, he toured Europe, the United States, and Australia, and became the first Indian to compose music for non-Indian films.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghoshp57_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghoshp57-14">[14]</a></sup> Chatur Lal accompanied Shankar on <i>tabla</i> until 1962, when Alla Rakha assumed the role.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip61_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip61-24">[24]</a></sup> Shankar founded the Kinnara School of Music in <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a> in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-Brockhaus_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brockhaus-25">[25]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Shankar befriended Richard Bock, founder of <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Jazz_Records" title="Pacific Jazz Records">World Pacific Records</a>, on his first American tour and recorded most of his albums in the 1950s and 1960s for Bock's label.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip61_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip61-24">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Byrds" title="The Byrds">The Byrds</a> recorded at the same studio and heard Shankar's music, which led them to incorporate some of its elements in theirs, introducing the genre to their friend George Harrison of the Beatles.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip62_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip62-26">[26]</a></sup> Harrison became interested in Indian classical music, bought a <i>sitar</i> and used it to record the song "<a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Wood_(This_Bird_Has_Flown)" title="Norwegian Wood (This Bird Has Flown)">Norwegian Wood (This Bird Has Flown)</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Schaffner_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schaffner-27">[27]</a></sup> This led to Indian music being used by other musicians and created the <a href="/wiki/Raga_rock" title="Raga rock">raga rock</a> trend.<sup id="cite_ref-Schaffner_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schaffner-27">[27]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Harrison met Shankar in London in June 1966 and visited India later that year for six weeks to study <i>sitar</i> under Shankar in <a href="/wiki/Srinagar" title="Srinagar">Srinagar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Arunabha_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arunabha-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Glass_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glass-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kozinn_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kozinn-29">[29]</a></sup> During the visit, a documentary film about Shankar named <a href="/wiki/Raga_(film)" title="Raga (film)"><i>Raga</i></a> was shot by Howard Worth, and released in 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Shankar's association with Harrison greatly increased Shankar's popularity and Ken Hunt of <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> would state that Shankar had become "the most famous Indian musician on the planet" by 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-AMG_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMG-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Glass_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glass-28">[28]</a></sup> In 1967, he performed at the <a href="/wiki/Monterey_Pop_Festival" title="Monterey Pop Festival">Monterey Pop Festival</a><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> and won a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Chamber_Music_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Chamber Music Performance">Grammy Award for Best Chamber Music Performance</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/West_Meets_East" title="West Meets East">West Meets East</a></i>, a collaboration with Yehudi Menuhin.<sup id="cite_ref-Glass_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glass-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Grammy_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy-32">[32]</a></sup> The same year, the Beatles won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Grammy Award for Album of the Year</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i>, which included "<a href="/wiki/Within_You_Without_You" title="Within You Without You">Within You Without You</a>" by Harrison, a song that was influenced by Indian classical music.<sup id="cite_ref-Kozinn_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kozinn-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Grammy_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy-32">[32]</a></sup> Shankar opened a Western branch of the Kinnara School of Music in Los Angeles, in May 1967, and published an autobiography, <i>My Music, My Life</i>, in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghoshp57_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghoshp57-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brockhaus_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brockhaus-25">[25]</a></sup> In 1968, he scored for the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Charly" title="Charly">Charly</a></i>. He performed at the <a href="/wiki/Woodstock_Festival" title="Woodstock Festival" class="mw-redirect">Woodstock Festival</a> in August 1969, and found he disliked the venue.<sup id="cite_ref-Glass_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glass-28">[28]</a></sup> In the 1970s Shankar distanced himself from the <a href="/wiki/Hippie" title="Hippie">hippie</a> movement.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahony_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahony-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970.E2.80.932012:_International_career">1970–2012: International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1970–2012: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:George_Harrison,_Gerald_Ford,_Ravi_Shankar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/George_Harrison%2C_Gerald_Ford%2C_Ravi_Shankar.jpg/220px-George_Harrison%2C_Gerald_Ford%2C_Ravi_Shankar.jpg" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/George_Harrison%2C_Gerald_Ford%2C_Ravi_Shankar.jpg/330px-George_Harrison%2C_Gerald_Ford%2C_Ravi_Shankar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/George_Harrison%2C_Gerald_Ford%2C_Ravi_Shankar.jpg/440px-George_Harrison%2C_Gerald_Ford%2C_Ravi_Shankar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3842" data-file-height="3043"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:George_Harrison,_Gerald_Ford,_Ravi_Shankar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a>, US President 
        <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a>, and Ravi Shankar in the Oval Office in December 1974
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In October 1970 Shankar became chair of the department of Indian music of the <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_the_Arts" title="California Institute of the Arts">California Institute of the Arts</a> after previously teaching at the <a href="/wiki/City_College_of_New_York" title="City College of New York">City College of New York</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Los_Angeles" title="University of California, Los Angeles">University of California, Los Angeles</a>, and being guest lecturer at other colleges and universities, including the <a href="/wiki/Ali_Akbar_College_of_Music" title="Ali Akbar College of Music">Ali Akbar College of Music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghoshp57_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghoshp57-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ghoshp56_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghoshp56-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip66_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip66-36">[36]</a></sup> In late 1970, the <a href="/wiki/London_Symphony_Orchestra" title="London Symphony Orchestra">London Symphony Orchestra</a> invited Shankar to compose a concerto with <i>sitar</i>. <i><a href="/wiki/Concerto_for_Sitar_%26_Orchestra" title="Concerto for Sitar &amp; Orchestra">Concerto for Sitar &amp; Orchestra</a></i> was performed with <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Previn" title="André Previn">André Previn</a> as conductor and Shankar playing the <i>sitar</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Massey_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Massey-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip221_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip221-37">[37]</a></sup> Hans Neuhoff of <i><a href="/wiki/Musik_in_Geschichte_und_Gegenwart" title="Musik in Geschichte und Gegenwart">Musik in Geschichte und Gegenwart</a></i> has criticized the usage of the orchestra in this concert as "amateurish".<sup id="cite_ref-Neuhoff_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neuhoff-38">[38]</a></sup> George Harrison organized the charity <a href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_Bangladesh" title="The Concert for Bangladesh">Concert for Bangladesh</a> in August 1971, in which Shankar participated.<sup id="cite_ref-Glass_28-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glass-28">[28]</a></sup> After the musicians had tuned up on stage for over a minute, the crowd broke into applause, to which the amused Shankar responded: "If you like our tuning so much, I hope you will enjoy the playing more."<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Although interest in Indian music had decreased in the early 1970s, the <a href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_Bangladesh_(album)" title="The Concert for Bangladesh (album)">concert album</a> became one of the best-selling recordings to feature the genre and won Shankar a second Grammy Award.<sup id="cite_ref-Grammy_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip66_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip66-36">[36]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>During the 1970s, Shankar and Harrison worked together again, recording <i><a href="/wiki/Shankar_Family_%26_Friends" title="Shankar Family &amp; Friends">Shankar Family &amp; Friends</a></i> in 1973 and touring North America the following year to a mixed response after Shankar had toured Europe with the Harrison-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Ravi_Shankar%27s_Music_Festival_from_India" title="Ravi Shankar's Music Festival from India">Music Festival from India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip195_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip195-40">[40]</a></sup> The demanding schedule weakened Shankar, and he suffered a heart attack in Chicago in November 1974, causing him to miss a portion of the tour.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip196_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip196-41">[41]</a></sup> In his absence, Shankar's sister-in-law, singer <a href="/wiki/Lakshmi_Shankar" title="Lakshmi Shankar">Lakshmi Shankar</a>, conducted the touring orchestra.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip196_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip196-41">[41]</a></sup> The touring band visited the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> on invitation of <a href="/wiki/John_Gardner_Ford" title="John Gardner Ford">John Gardner Ford</a>, son of US President <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip196_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip196-41">[41]</a></sup> Shankar toured and taught for the remainder of the 1970s and the 1980s and released his second concerto, <i>Raga Mala</i>, conducted by <a href="/wiki/Zubin_Mehta" title="Zubin Mehta">Zubin Mehta</a>, in 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip222_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip222-43">[43]</a></sup> Shankar was nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Music_Score" title="Academy Award for Best Original Music Score" class="mw-redirect">Academy Award for Best Original Music Score</a> for his work on the 1982 movie <i><a href="/wiki/Gandhi_(film)" title="Gandhi (film)">Gandhi</a></i>, but lost to <a href="/wiki/John_Williams" title="John Williams">John Williams</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/E.T._the_Extra-Terrestrial" title="E.T. the Extra-Terrestrial">ET</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Oscar_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oscar-44">[44]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>He served as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Rajya_Sabha" title="Rajya Sabha">Rajya Sabha</a>, the upper chamber of the Parliament of India, from 12 May 1986 to 11 May 1992, after being nominated by Indian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Rajiv_Gandhi" title="Rajiv Gandhi">Rajiv Gandhi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Arunabha_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arunabha-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Shankar composed the dance drama <i>Ghanashyam</i> in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-Brockhaus_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brockhaus-25">[25]</a></sup> His liberal views on musical co-operation led him to contemporary composer <a href="/wiki/Philip_Glass" title="Philip Glass">Philip Glass</a>, with whom he released an album, <i><a href="/wiki/Passages_(Ravi_Shankar_and_Philip_Glass_album)" title="Passages (Ravi Shankar and Philip Glass album)">Passages</a></i>, in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGrove_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGrove-8">[8]</a></sup> Shankar underwent an <a href="/wiki/Angioplasty" title="Angioplasty">angioplasty</a> in 1992 due to heart problems, after which George Harrison participated in a number of Shankar's projects.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip197_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip197-46">[46]</a></sup> Because of the positive response to Shankar's 1996 career compilation <i><a href="/wiki/Ravi_Shankar:_In_Celebration" title="Ravi Shankar: In Celebration">In Celebration</a></i>, Shankar wrote a second autobiography, <i><a href="/wiki/Raga_Mala_(book)" title="Raga Mala (book)">Raga Mala</a></i>, with Harrison as editor.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip197_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip197-46">[46]</a></sup> He performed in between 25 and 40 concerts every year during the late 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGrove_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGrove-8">[8]</a></sup> Shankar taught his daughter Anoushka Shankar to play <i>sitar</i> and in 1997 became a Regents' Professor at <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Diego" title="University of California, San Diego">University of California, San Diego</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In the 2000s, he won a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_World_Music_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best World Music Album">Grammy Award for Best World Music Album</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Full_Circle:_Carnegie_Hall_2000" title="Full Circle: Carnegie Hall 2000">Full Circle: Carnegie Hall 2000</a></i> and toured with Anoushka, who released a book about her father, <i>Bapi: Love of My Life</i>, in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-Grammy_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip417_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip417-49">[49]</a></sup> Anoushka performed a composition by Shankar for the 2002 Harrison memorial <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_George" title="Concert for George">Concert for George</a> and Shankar wrote a third concerto for <i>sitar</i> and orchestra for Anoushka and the <a href="/wiki/Orpheus_Chamber_Orchestra" title="Orpheus Chamber Orchestra">Orpheus Chamber Orchestra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In June 2008, Shankar played what was billed as his last European concert,<sup id="cite_ref-Mahony_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahony-33">[33]</a></sup> but his 2011 tour included dates in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On 1 July 2010, at the <a href="/wiki/Southbank_Centre" title="Southbank Centre">Southbank Centre</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Royal_Festival_Hall" title="Royal Festival Hall">Royal Festival Hall</a>, London, England, <a href="/wiki/Anoushka_Shankar" title="Anoushka Shankar">Anoushka Shankar</a>, on sitar, performed with the <a href="/wiki/London_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="London Philharmonic Orchestra">London Philharmonic Orchestra</a>, conducted by David Murphy what was billed the first <i>Symphony</i> by Ravi Shankar. This performance was recorded and is available on CD. It is 40:52 minutes long and is composed of 4 movements (in the <a href="/wiki/Tempo_(music)" title="Tempo (music)" class="mw-redirect">tempi</a> allegro (fast), slow, scherzo (fast), finale (fast)) like a classical Western <a href="/wiki/Symphony" title="Symphony">symphony</a> but uses an Indian <a href="/wiki/Raga" title="Raga">raga</a> as the mode for each movement: I. Allegro (Kafi Zila) 9:21 minutes, II. Lento (Ahir Bhairav) 7:52 minutes, III. Scherzo (DoGa Kalyan) 8:49 minutes IV. Finale (Banjara) 14:50 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The website of the Ravi Shankar Foundation provides the information that "The symphony was written in Indian notation in 2010, and has been interpreted by his student and conductor, David Murphy."<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The information available on the website does not explain this process of "interpretation" of Ravi Shankar's notation by David Murphy, nor how Ravi Shankar's Indian notation could accommodate Western orchestral writing.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_and_contributions">Style and contributions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Style and contributions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"> 
       <div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="<div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; style=&quot;width:480px&quot;><video id=&quot;mwe_player_1&quot; poster=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Ravi_Shankar_-_Madhuvanti.ogg/480px--Ravi_Shankar_-_Madhuvanti.ogg.jpg&quot;         <i><a href="/wiki/Madhuvanti" title="Madhuvanti">Madhuvanti</a></i> at the

     <p>Shankar developed a style distinct from that of his contemporaries and incorporated influences from rhythm practices of <a href="/wiki/Carnatic_music" title="Carnatic music">Carnatic music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGrove_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGrove-8">[8]</a></sup> His performances begin with solo <i><a href="/wiki/Alap" title="Alap">alap</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Jor_(music)" title="Jor (music)"><i>jor</i></a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Jhala" title="Jhala">jhala</a></i> (introduction and performances with pulse and rapid pulse) influenced by the slow and serious <i><a href="/wiki/Dhrupad" title="Dhrupad">dhrupad</a></i> genre, followed by a section with <i>tabla</i> accompaniment featuring compositions associated with the prevalent <i><a href="/wiki/Khyal" title="Khyal">khyal</a></i> style.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGrove_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGrove-8">[8]</a></sup> Shankar often closed his performances with a piece inspired by the light-classical <i><a href="/wiki/Thumri" title="Thumri">thumri</a></i> genre.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGrove_8-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGrove-8">[8]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Shankar has been considered one of the top <i>sitar</i> players of the second half of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Neuhoff_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neuhoff-38">[38]</a></sup> He popularised performing on the bass octave of the <i>sitar</i> for the <i>alap</i> section and became known for a distinctive playing style in the middle and high registers that used quick and short deviations of the playing string and his sound creation through stops and strikes on the main playing string.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGrove_8-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGrove-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Neuhoff_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neuhoff-38">[38]</a></sup> Narayana Menon of <a href="/wiki/Grove_Dictionary_of_Music_and_Musicians" title="Grove Dictionary of Music and Musicians" class="mw-redirect"><i>The New Grove Dictionary</i></a> noted Shankar's liking for rhythmic novelties, among them the use of unconventional rhythmic cycles.<sup id="cite_ref-Menon_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Menon-55">[55]</a></sup> Hans Neuhoff of <i><a href="/wiki/Musik_in_Geschichte_und_Gegenwart" title="Musik in Geschichte und Gegenwart">Musik in Geschichte und Gegenwart</a></i> has argued that Shankar's playing style was not widely adopted and that he was surpassed by other <i>sitar</i> players in the performance of melodic passages.<sup id="cite_ref-Neuhoff_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neuhoff-38">[38]</a></sup> Shankar's interplay with Alla Rakha improved appreciation for <i>tabla</i> playing in <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_classical_music" title="Hindustani classical music">Hindustani classical music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Neuhoff_38-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neuhoff-38">[38]</a></sup> Shankar promoted the <i><a href="/wiki/Jugalbandi" title="Jugalbandi">jugalbandi</a></i> duet concert style and claims to have introduced new ragas <i>Tilak Shyam</i>, <i>Nat Bhairav</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Bairagi" title="Bairagi">Bairagi</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGrove_8-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGrove-8">[8]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition">Recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indian_governmental_honours">Indian governmental honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Indian governmental honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Sangeet_Natak_Akademi_Award" title="Sangeet Natak Akademi Award">Sangeet Natak Akademi Award</a> (1962)<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Padma_Bhushan" title="Padma Bhushan">Padma Bhushan</a> (1967)<sup id="cite_ref-Padma_Awards_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Padma_Awards-57">[57]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Sangeet_Natak_Akademi_Fellowship" title="Sangeet Natak Akademi Fellowship">Sangeet Natak Akademi Fellowship</a> (1975).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Padma_Vibhushan" title="Padma Vibhushan">Padma Vibhushan</a> (1981)<sup id="cite_ref-Padma_Awards_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Padma_Awards-57">[57]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Kalidas_Samman" title="Kalidas Samman">Kalidas Samman</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Madhya_Pradesh" title="Government of Madhya Pradesh">Government of Madhya Pradesh</a> for 1987–88<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Bharat_Ratna" title="Bharat Ratna">Bharat Ratna</a> (1999)<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_governmental_and_academic_honours">Other governmental and academic honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other governmental and academic honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Ramon_Magsaysay_Award" title="Ramon Magsaysay Award">Ramon Magsaysay Award</a> (1992) and the .<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Commander of the <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9gion_d%27honneur" title="Légion d'honneur" class="mw-redirect">Legion of Honour</a> of France (2000)<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Honorary <a href="/wiki/Knight_Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Knight Commander of the Order of the British Empire" class="mw-redirect">Knight Commander of the Order of the British Empire</a> (KBE) by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> for "services to music" (2001)<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Honorary degrees from universities in India and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghoshp57_14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghoshp57-14">[14]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Honorary member of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Letters" title="American Academy of Arts and Letters">American Academy of Arts and Letters</a></li> 
      <li>Honorary Doctor of Laws from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Melbourne" title="University of Melbourne">University of Melbourne</a>, Australia (2010)<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_awards">Arts awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Arts awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li>1964 fellowship from the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Cultural_Council" title="Asian Cultural Council">John D. Rockefeller 3rd Fund</a></li> 
      <li>Silver Bear Extraordinary Prize of the Jury at the <a href="/wiki/7th_Berlin_International_Film_Festival" title="7th Berlin International Film Festival">1957 Berlin International Film Festival</a> (for composing the music for the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Kabuliwala" title="Kabuliwala" class="mw-redirect">Kabuliwala</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/International_Music_Council" title="International Music Council">International Music Council</a> (1975)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Fukuoka_Asian_Culture_Prize" title="Fukuoka Asian Culture Prize" class="mw-redirect">Fukuoka Asian Culture Prize</a> (1991)<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Praemium_Imperiale" title="Praemium Imperiale">Praemium Imperiale</a> for music from the Japan Art Association (1997)<sup id="cite_ref-NewGrove_8-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGrove-8">[8]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Polar_Music_Prize" title="Polar Music Prize">Polar Music Prize</a> (1998)<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Five <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a> 
       <ul> 
        <li>1967: Best Chamber Music Performance - West Meets East (with <a href="/wiki/Yehudi_Menuhin" title="Yehudi Menuhin">Yehudi Menuhin</a>)</li> 
        <li>1973: Album of the Year - <a href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_Bangladesh" title="The Concert for Bangladesh">The Concert for Bangladesh</a> (with <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a>)</li> 
        <li>2002: Best World Music Album - Full Circle: Carnegie Hall 2000</li> 
        <li>2013: Best World Music Album - The Living Room Sessions Pt. 1</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award">Lifetime Achievement Award</a> received at the <a href="/wiki/55th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="55th Annual Grammy Awards">55th Annual Grammy Awards</a><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></li> 
       </ul> </li> 
      <li>Nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award" class="mw-redirect">Academy Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghoshp57_14-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghoshp57-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Grammy_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Oscar_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oscar-44">[44]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Posthumous nomination in the 56th Annual Grammy Awards for his album "The Living Room Sessions Part 2".<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>First recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Tagore_Award" title="Tagore Award">Tagore Award</a> in recognition of his outstanding contribution to cultural harmony and universal values (2013; posthumous)<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_honours_and_tributes">Other honours and tributes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other honours and tributes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li>American jazz saxophonist <a href="/wiki/John_Coltrane" title="John Coltrane">John Coltrane</a> named his son <a href="/wiki/Ravi_Coltrane" title="Ravi Coltrane">Ravi Coltrane</a> after Shankar.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>On April 7, 2016 Google published a Google Doodle to honor his work.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life_and_family">Personal life and family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personal life and family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p>Shankar married Allauddin Khan's daughter <a href="/wiki/Annapurna_Devi" title="Annapurna Devi">Annapurna Devi</a> in 1941 and their son, <a href="/wiki/Shubhendra_Shankar" title="Shubhendra Shankar">Shubhendra Shankar</a>, was born in 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-Lavezzolip52_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavezzolip52-12">[12]</a></sup> Shankar separated from Devi during the 1940s and had a relationship with <a href="/wiki/Kamala_Shastri" title="Kamala Shastri" class="mw-redirect">Kamala Shastri</a>, a dancer, beginning in the late 1940s.<sup id="cite_ref-PTI030513_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PTI030513-73">[73]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>An affair with Sue Jones, a New York concert producer, led to the birth of <a href="/wiki/Norah_Jones" title="Norah Jones">Norah Jones</a> in 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-PTI030513_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PTI030513-73">[73]</a></sup> He separated from Shastri in 1981 and lived with Sue until 1986.</p> 
     <p>In 1989 he married Sukanya Rajan, whom he had known since the 1970s,<sup id="cite_ref-PTI030513_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PTI030513-73">[73]</a></sup> at <a href="/wiki/Chilkur_Temple" title="Chilkur Temple" class="mw-redirect">Chilkur Temple</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad,_India" title="Hyderabad, India" class="mw-redirect">Hyderabad, India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Their daughter <a href="/wiki/Anoushka_Shankar" title="Anoushka Shankar">Anoushka Shankar</a> was born in 1981.</p> 
     <p>Shankar's son, Shubhendra "Shubho" Shankar, often accompanied him on tours.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT920921_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT920921-75">[75]</a></sup> He could play the <i>sitar</i> and <i>surbahar</i>, but elected not to pursue a solo career. Shubhendra died of pneumonia in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT920921_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT920921-75">[75]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Ananda_Shankar" title="Ananda Shankar">Ananda Shankar</a>, the experimental fusion musician, is his nephew.</p> 
     <p>Norah Jones became a successful musician in the 2000s, winning eight Grammy Awards in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-Venugopal_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Venugopal-76">[76]</a></sup> Anoushka Shankar was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_World_Music_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best World Music Album">Grammy Award for Best World Music Album</a> in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-Venugopal_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Venugopal-76">[76]</a></sup> Anoushka and her father were both nominated for Best World Music Album at the <a href="/wiki/2013_Grammy_Awards" title="2013 Grammy Awards" class="mw-redirect">2013 Grammy Awards</a> for separate albums.<sup id="cite_ref-2013grammynom_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013grammynom-77">[77]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Shankar was a <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu</a>, and a devotee of the Hindu deity, <a href="/wiki/Hanuman" title="Hanuman">Hanuman</a>. As well, he was an "ardent" devotee of the revered, Bengali Hindu saint, <a href="/wiki/Anandamayi_Ma" title="Anandamayi Ma">Sri Anandamayi Ma</a>. Shankar used to visit Anandamayi Ma frequently and performed for her on various occasions. Shankar wrote of his hometown, Varanasi, and his initial encounter with "Ma": <sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p>"<a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">Varanasi</a> is the eternal abode of Lord Shiva, and one of my favorite temples is that of Lord <a href="/wiki/Hanuman" title="Hanuman">Hanuman</a>, the monkey god. The city is also where one of the miracles that have happened in my life took place: I met Ma Anandamayi, a great spiritual soul. Seeing the beauty of her face and mind, I became her ardent devotee. Sitting at home now in Encinitas, in Southern California, at the age of 88, surrounded by the beautiful greens, multi-colored flowers, blue sky, clean air, and the Pacific Ocean, I often reminisce about all the wonderful places I have seen in the world. I cherish the memories of Paris, New York, and a few other places. But Varanasi seems to be etched in my heart!"</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>In his later years, Shankar became a vegetarian.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> He wore a large diamond ring which he said was "manifested" by <a href="/wiki/Sathya_Sai_Baba" title="Sathya Sai Baba">Sathya Sai Baba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> He lived with Sukanya in <a href="/wiki/Encinitas" title="Encinitas" class="mw-redirect">Encinitas, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Shankar performed his final concert, with daughter Anoushka, on 4 November 2012 at the <a href="/wiki/Terrace_Theater" title="Terrace Theater">Terrace Theater</a> in <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach,_California" title="Long Beach, California">Long Beach, California</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Illness_and_death">Illness and death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Illness and death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p>On 6 December 2012, Shankar was admitted to <a href="/wiki/Scripps_Health" title="Scripps Health">Scripps Memorial Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/La_Jolla,_San_Diego,_California" title="La Jolla, San Diego, California" class="mw-redirect">La Jolla, San Diego, California</a> after complaining of breathing difficulties. He died on 11 December 2012 at around 16:30 <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Standard_Time" title="Pacific Standard Time" class="mw-redirect">PST</a> after undergoing heart valve replacement surgery.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Swara_Samrat_festival" title="Swara Samrat festival">Swara Samrat festival</a></i> organized on 5–6 January 2013 was dedicated to Ravi Shankar and <a href="/wiki/Ali_Akbar_Khan" title="Ali Akbar Khan">Ali Akbar Khan</a> where musicians like <a href="/wiki/Shivkumar_Sharma" title="Shivkumar Sharma">Shivkumar Sharma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birju_Maharaj" title="Birju Maharaj">Birju Maharaj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hari_Prasad_Chaurasia" title="Hari Prasad Chaurasia" class="mw-redirect">Hari Prasad Chaurasia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zakir_Hussain_(musician)" title="Zakir Hussain (musician)">Zakir Hussain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Girija_Devi" title="Girija Devi">Girija Devi</a> performed.<sup id="cite_ref-Classical_legends_leave_their_mark_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Classical_legends_leave_their_mark-84">[84]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ravi_Shankar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
